  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f00720d8-09dd-4f2a-a070-b57c9864ead8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8249776314214190833">Milk and honey' is a collection of poetry and prose about survival. About the experience of violence, abuse, love, loss, and femininity. It is split into four chapters, and each chapter serves a different purpose. Deals with a different pain. Heals a different heartache. 'milk and honey' takes readers through a journey of the most bitter moments in life and finds sweetness</span>
  <span id="freeText8249776314214190833" style="display:none">Milk and honey' is a collection of poetry and prose about survival. About the experience of violence, abuse, love, loss, and femininity. It is split into four chapters, and each chapter serves a different purpose. Deals with a different pain. Heals a different heartache. 'milk and honey' takes readers through a journey of the most bitter moments in life and finds sweetness in them because there is sweetness everywhere if you are just willing to look.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8249776314214190833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There are zero pages of poetry in this book. There are 208 pages of excerpts from someone's diary, with oddly placed line breaks, occasional doodles a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There are zero pages of poetry in this book. There are 208 pages of excerpts from someone's diary, with oddly placed line breaks, occasional doodles and chapters with theme names, so you'll know which emotions the author is trying to squeeze out of you.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/640216-can-anyone-tell-me-the-age-appropriateness">Can anyone tell me the age-appropriateness for this title? I had a student request it for a high school library, and while it is obviously a very powerful read, I am wondering if it may be too mature and/or beyond the scope of our target patronage.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_640216'><a id="like_count_community_question_640216" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/640216?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">28 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F23513349-milk-and-honey">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6000864-melanie"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1600583306i/6000864._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6000864-melanie">Melanie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The author is writing about experiences that occurred throughout her then-21 years of experience. I believe it to be appropriate for a high school lib<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The author is writing about experiences that occurred throughout her then-21 years of experience. I believe it to be appropriate for a high school library, not because they may find the trauma, raw sexuality, and stark feminism shocking...but because they may find it FAMILIAR. <br /><br />This book is about acknowledging the hurt done to us by ourselves and others, and how to go about healing those hurts. I don't believe that is something that should be censored. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <span id="freeText6338092986035232269" style="display:none"><i> 2 stars for the beautiful thoughts. </i> <br /><br />So if I write my review<br />like this<br />will it <br />automatically<br />become poetry?<br />In my humble opinion<br />this book is<br />composed of <br />extremely beautifully<br />written lines<br />but there are very<br />few <br />poems <br />actually.<br />what i dont <br />understand <br />is why<br />why <br />you have to<br />click the enter key<br />to make it look<br />beautiful <br />when u can <br />continue <br />the same line<br />same paragraph <br />same page<br />also <br />why a published book<br />gives no shit<br />about<br />capitalizing 'i'<br />is <br />beyond me<br /><br />Consider this line from Milk and Honey: <br /><b>“you might not have been my first love<br />but you were the love that made <br />all other loves seem <br />irrelevant” </b><br /><br />write it without clicking enter<br /><b>“you might not have been my first love but you were the love that made all other loves seem irrelevant” </b><br /><br />Now consider this line from the novel The Wrath And The Dawn:<br /><b>“People fall in and out of love with the rising and setting of the sun.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1530502641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5020200198333327076">2/7/2017<br/>I get likes on this review daily and for a long time i've felt like a 3-star review was too generous so I lowered it to 2 today, which is more accurate in hindsight.<br/><br/>7/11/2016<br/>If I could sum up my thoughts about this book, it would just be, "Oh."<br/><br/>Honestly, very underwhelming. I'm not sure why people go crazy about this book and say it's gorgeous and it's their favorite book, because honestly, it's very plain. Some poems are just basic sentences with random skips that have no real point, the</span>
  <span id="freeText5020200198333327076" style="display:none">2/7/2017<br />I get likes on this review daily and for a long time i've felt like a 3-star review was too generous so I lowered it to 2 today, which is more accurate in hindsight.<br /><br />7/11/2016<br />If I could sum up my thoughts about this book, it would just be, "Oh."<br /><br />Honestly, very underwhelming. I'm not sure why people go crazy about this book and say it's gorgeous and it's their favorite book, because honestly, it's very plain. Some poems are just basic sentences with random skips that have no real point, they aren't too lyrical, and it's literally just like reading a normal sentence. I expected I would love every page of this, but I only marked 4 poems. This just was nothing new. The concepts in this poem, especially when it rolled around to the feminism aspects, just didn't wow me. An entire poem just about "you don't NEED a man you WANT a man" was just a repeat of things I've been hearing for years. It wasn't interesting, and a lot of the poems just sounded so pretentious because it was just plain text with no punctuation and random skips in the lines being fed to the reader as art. Someone mentioned this was a little too "Tumblr," and I agree. It was a quick read, but just a little bit frustrating because it was too simple, too familiar. The art was nice and a few of the poems were well-written, but for the most part, it seems like very little effort was put into this, which makes me sad because that's such a mean criticism for an artist who puts so much emotion into her work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5020200198333327076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1561218333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12671855813663087994">I read this in a bookshop. I wanted to give it zero stars. It's not poetry. It's shamefully derivitive and doesn't employ any poetic devices except for the most cliched - and not to positive effect. Random line breaks and sentence fragments are used because it is what is expected of a poem, but the author doesn't seem to understand that in poetry, these serve a purpose and must contribute to the poem's larger meaning. The allusions and metaphors are misplaced and nonsensical. "Milk and honey" is</span>
  <span id="freeText12671855813663087994" style="display:none">I read this in a bookshop. I wanted to give it zero stars. It's not poetry. It's shamefully derivitive and doesn't employ any poetic devices except for the most cliched - and not to positive effect. Random line breaks and sentence fragments are used because it is what is expected of a poem, but the author doesn't seem to understand that in poetry, these serve a purpose and must contribute to the poem's larger meaning. The allusions and metaphors are misplaced and nonsensical. "Milk and honey" is a phrase that has been used for hundreds if not thousands of years: there is nothing new or interesting or creative or poetic in this book. It reads like a 13 year old's diary. This book is for people who have never read poetry outside of school, and that's too bad. I feel sorry for them because they are missing out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12671855813663087994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5263999531877954390">While Rupi Kaur seems very passionate and while I agree with her politics, content, and message, that doesn't make this writing very good. Some of the poems are excellent and will draw you in, but mainly, they are very overrated in terms of pure quality. I see why her poems are popular, but not why she's considered a 'great' or 'brilliant' writer. She's addressing universal themes, but she doesn't do so in an especially artful/skilled way. I'd say if you aren't a big fan of poetry, this book cou</span>
  <span id="freeText5263999531877954390" style="display:none">While Rupi Kaur seems very passionate and while I agree with her politics, content, and message, that doesn't make this writing very good. Some of the poems are excellent and will draw you in, but mainly, they are very overrated in terms of pure quality. I see why her poems are popular, but not why she's considered a 'great' or 'brilliant' writer. She's addressing universal themes, but she doesn't do so in an especially artful/skilled way. I'd say if you aren't a big fan of poetry, this book could get you interested in it, but if you're expecting just plain good old-fashioned literary talent, you won't find it here.</span>

<div id="review_1855783680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1855783680" />
    <a title="Ariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530557165p2/6536286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1855783680?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1855783680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10496860877991163484">2016 was a year of poetry for me. I read more poetry than I ever have before, I wrote more poetry than I knew I was capable of, and I even started performing poetry. Milk and Honey was one of the catalysts for this, written by an author from a town near me, of very similar age to me, powerful and raw, I enjoyed flipping through this and connecting to the poems and illustrations. I like that she shares her poetry online, that a huge part of why they're successful is because of how sharable they a</span>
  <span id="freeText10496860877991163484" style="display:none">2016 was a year of poetry for me. I read more poetry than I ever have before, I wrote more poetry than I knew I was capable of, and I even started performing poetry. Milk and Honey was one of the catalysts for this, written by an author from a town near me, of very similar age to me, powerful and raw, I enjoyed flipping through this and connecting to the poems and illustrations. I like that she shares her poetry online, that a huge part of why they're successful is because of how sharable they are. I like that they were about abuse and healing, but also about love and self love. I see this book as a great inspiration, I see Rupi Kaur as a great inspiration, and I'm glad it was a big part of my thoughts in 2016.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483047648i/21575034._SX540_.jpg" width="600" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This was me after performing at an event in Brampton, Ontario on April 11th, 2016 with Rupi Kaur!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=poetry-and-verse-novels">poetry-and-verse-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2017">read2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1886864660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6470918046790184001">Some people call this poetry. I call it a bunch of pretty quotes from Tumblr or Pinterest or other similar site. <br/><br/>The themes covered are incredibly relevant. And <b>highly</b> emotive which is probably why so many people connect with this collection. <br/>But in my opinion there is a difference in saying/telling what you feel and in writing/showing what you feel. This was a bunch of very quotable quotes about subject matters that need to be explored, and put front and centre into the public mindset, but <b>with</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6470918046790184001" style="display:none">Some people call this poetry. I call it a bunch of pretty quotes from Tumblr or Pinterest or other similar site. <br /><br />The themes covered are incredibly relevant. And <b>highly</b> emotive which is probably why so many people connect with this collection. <br />But in my opinion there is a difference in saying/telling what you feel and in writing/showing what you feel. This was a bunch of very quotable quotes about subject matters that need to be explored, and put front and centre into the public mindset, but <b>without</b> the lyricism of poetry. So I'm rating this not on the themes covered but on the prose. <br /><br />Maybe I'm harsh with my rating. I have plenty of GR friends whose opinions I value that absolutely adored this. Guess I'm just old fashioned when it comes to poetry. And I'm okay with that. <br /><br /><b>One star</b> </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer2772836575968865943"><b>milk and honey</b> is a collection of poetry and prose about survival. About the experience of violence, abuse, love, loss, and femininity. It is split into four chapters, and each chapter serves a different purpose. <br/><br/>It’s difficult trying to review this because every poem is extremely personal, tender and exquisite in its own way.<br/><br/>So I decided to feature some of my favorite ones:<br/><br/><i>“you tell me to quiet down cause<br/>my opinions make me less beautiful<br/>but i was not made with a fire in my belly<br/>so i could be p</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2772836575968865943" style="display:none"><b>milk and honey</b> is a collection of poetry and prose about survival. About the experience of violence, abuse, love, loss, and femininity. It is split into four chapters, and each chapter serves a different purpose. <br><br>It’s difficult trying to review this because every poem is extremely personal, tender and exquisite in its own way.<br><br>So I decided to feature some of my favorite ones:<br><br><i>“you tell me to quiet down cause<br>my opinions make me less beautiful<br>but i was not made with a fire in my belly<br>so i could be put out<br>i was not made with a lightness on my tongue<br>so i could be easy to swallow<br>i was made heavy<br>half blade and half silk<br>difficult to forget and not easy<br>for the mind to follow”<br><br>“i struggle so deeply<br>to understand<br>how someone can<br>pour their entire soul<br>blood and energy<br>into someone<br>without wanting<br>anything in<br>return<br><br>- i will have to wait till i’m a mother”<br><br>“when my mother says i deserve better<br>i snap to your defense out of habit<br>he still loves me i shout<br>she looks at me with defeated eyes<br>the way a parent looks at their child<br>when they know this is the type of pain<br>even they can’t fix<br>and says<br>it means nothing to me if he loves you<br>if he can’t do a single wretched thing about it”<br><br>“he only whispers i love you<br>as he slips his hands<br>down the waistband<br>of your pants<br><br>this is where you must<br>understand the difference<br>between want and need<br>you may want that boy<br>but you certainly<br>don’t need him”<br><br>“i am a museum full of art<br>but you had your eyes shut”<br><br>“people go<br>but how<br>they left<br>always stays”<br><br>“what i miss most is how you loved me. but what i didn’t know was how you loved me had so much to do with the person i was. it was a reflection of everything i gave to you. coming back to me. how did i not see that. how. did i sit here soaking in the idea that no one else would love me that way. when it was i that taught you. when it was i that showed you how to fill. the way i needed to be filled. how cruel i was to myself. giving you credit for my warmth simply because you had felt it. thinking it was you who gave me strength. wit. beauty. simply because you recognized it. as if i was already not these things before i met you. as if i did not remain all these once you left.”<br><br>“loneliness is a sign you are in desperate need of yourself”<br><br>“you tell me<br>i am not like most girls<br>and learn to kiss me with your eyes closed<br>something about the phrase—something about<br>how i have to be unlike the women<br>i call sisters in order to be wanted<br>makes me want to spit your tongue out<br>like i am supposed to be proud you picked me<br>as if i should be relieved you think<br>i am better than them”<br><br>“other women’s bodies<br>are not our battlegrounds”<br><br>“you were a dragon long before<br>he came around and said<br>you could fly<br><br>you will remain a dragon<br>long after he’s left”<br><br>“you look at me and cry<br>everything hurts<br><br>i hold you and whisper<br>but everything can heal”<br><br>“how you love yourself is<br>how you teach others<br>to love you”<br><br>“what terrifies me most is how we<br>foam at the mouth with envy<br>when others succeed<br>but sigh in relief<br>when they are failing<br><br>our struggle to<br>celebrate each other is<br>what’s proven most difficult<br>in being human”</i><br><br>(Most of my favorite quotes were from <b>the healing</b> section, and it was pretty though trying to narrow it down to my preferred quotes.)<br><br>It also featured some pretty amazing illustrations, which I’m always up for in <div id="review_1419362679" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1419362679" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1419362679?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Thomas by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/21052508-gagan">Gagan</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-physical">own-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1419362679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer607003519879977744"><i>milk and honey</i> tore through my analytical mind and burrowed deep into my ultra-sensitive soul. It slayed all my emotions, my feminist desires, and my love for vulnerable writing. I may not know a lot about poetry, but I do know a decent amount about feelings, and Rupi Kaur brought all my feelings tumbling out with this gorgeous collection of poems. She writes about love and loss, trauma, and femininity - subjects that I so happen to adore. In spare yet thorough language, she addresses what it fe</span>
  <span id="freeText607003519879977744" style="display:none"><i>milk and honey</i> tore through my analytical mind and burrowed deep into my ultra-sensitive soul. It slayed all my emotions, my feminist desires, and my love for vulnerable writing. I may not know a lot about poetry, but I do know a decent amount about feelings, and Rupi Kaur brought all my feelings tumbling out with this gorgeous collection of poems. She writes about love and loss, trauma, and femininity - subjects that I so happen to adore. In spare yet thorough language, she addresses what it feels like to be broken, to be loved, and to be stronger on one's own. This collection, while in many ways simple, addresses some of the darkest and most hopeful matters of the human heart. If you enjoy marinating in your feelings or if you often ponder topics like female empowerment, getting over heartbreak, or what it means to love, I would recommend you check out <i>milk and honey</i> asap. Now I will include three of my favorite poems, though I wish I could include them all.<br /><br />On calling women pretty:<br />"i want to apologize to all the women<br />i have called pretty<br />before i've called them intelligent or brave<br />i am sorry i made it sound as though<br />something as simple as what you're born with<br />is the most you have to be proud of when your<br />spirit has crushed mountains<br />from now on i will say things like<br /><i>you are resilient</i> or <i>you are extraordinary</i><br />not because i don't think you're pretty<br />but because you are so much more than that"<br /><br />On co-dependency:<br />"you are in the habit<br />of co-depending<br />on people to<br />make up for what<br />you think you lack<br /><br />who tricked you<br />into believing<br />another person<br />was meant to complete you<br />when the most they can do is complement"<br /><br />On what is most important:<br />"most importantly love<br />like it's the only thing you know how<br />at the end of the day all this<br />means nothing<br />this page<br />where you're sitting<br />your degree<br />your job<br />the money<br />nothing even matters<br />except love and human connection<br />who you loved<br />and how deeply you loved them<br />how you touched the people around you<br />and how much you gave them"</span>
  <a data-text-id="607003519879977744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17731016313542305984" style="display:none"><i>“i am a museum full of art<br />but you had your eyes shut”</i><br /><br />Wow. Rupi Kaur really touched me deeply with this incredibly work of art. Her words of truth and honesty are so powerful and so full of emotion, I can't imagine anyone's eyes staying dry while reading it.<br />A few times, though, I was a little confused, I couldn't comprehend the meaning of her words. The again came a poem about independence, how she was healing from her boyfriend's loss, closely followed by one that showed her hopeless and lost once again.<br />Anyway, this was so much more complex than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30075802.The_Princess_Saves_Herself_in_this_One" title="The Princess Saves Herself in this One by Amanda Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Saves Herself in this One</a>, but however different these two books are, they both have their own power and strength.<br /><br />Here is one more poem taken from <i>Milk and Honey</i> that I can't stop thinking about:<br /><br /><i>“i want to apologize to all the women i have called pretty before i’ve called them intelligent or brave i am sorry i made it sound as though something as simple as what you’re born with is the most you have to be proud of when your spirit has crushed mountains from now on i will say things like you are resilient or you are extraordinary not because i don’t think you’re pretty but because you are so much more than that”</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1713906719" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1713906719?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713906719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer415142831228450765">Breathtaking - Brutal - Beautiful<br/><br/>Rupi Kaur's poetry is unlike traditional poetry. For one thing - this small book feels like a graphic poetry novel. <br/>Many of the pages had a familiar 'looking-style' which short poems have....but with the delicate, simple, drawings, I forgot I was reading poetry. The drawings tell a story --we feel the emotions from the them before we even read the words. In essence, <br/>capturing bruises women have experienced. <br/><br/>The book is divided into four sections: hurting, loving,</span>
  <span id="freeText415142831228450765" style="display:none">Breathtaking - Brutal - Beautiful<br /><br />Rupi Kaur's poetry is unlike traditional poetry. For one thing - this small book feels like a graphic poetry novel. <br />Many of the pages had a familiar 'looking-style' which short poems have....but with the delicate, simple, drawings, I forgot I was reading poetry. The drawings tell a story --we feel the emotions from the them before we even read the words. In essence, <br />capturing bruises women have experienced. <br /><br />The book is divided into four sections: hurting, loving, breaking, healing.<br />This book honors women.....addressing chaos with compassion....love, loss, trauma, abuse, healing, and femininity.<br /><br />It's real. It's raw. It's relatable. <br /><br />I say again.... 'beautiful'<br /><br />"If you were born with<br />the weakness to fall<br />you were born with<br />the strength to rise".<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="415142831228450765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=what-a-pointless-book">what-a-pointless-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3595074758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2594001775905203780">*laughs awkwardly* That just happened. <br/><br/>If I had known I could write a bestselling book of poetry by putting random thoughts on blank paper and making them look ~pretty,~ I would be a millionaire by now. <br/><br/>i don't understand<br/>the point <br/>of breaking sentences<br/>up like this<br/>for the sake<br/>of wasting paper<br/>and my time<br/><br/>There. Was that poetry? Apparently. <br/><br/><i>Milk and Honey</i> is supposed to be inspiring and feminist. At least, that's what I read in the synopsis. I picked it up because of the memes, but whatever. It wasn</span>
  <span id="freeText2594001775905203780" style="display:none">*laughs awkwardly* That just happened. <br /><br />If I had known I could write a bestselling book of poetry by putting random thoughts on blank paper and making them look ~pretty,~ I would be a millionaire by now. <br /><br />i don't understand<br />the point <br />of breaking sentences<br />up like this<br />for the sake<br />of wasting paper<br />and my time<br /><br />There. Was that poetry? Apparently. <br /><br /><i>Milk and Honey</i> is supposed to be inspiring and feminist. At least, that's what I read in the synopsis. I picked it up because of the memes, but whatever. It wasn't inspiring, and it wasn't meme-worthy either. <br /><br />_<br /><br />i brought you <br />ice cream<br />but you were<br />lactose intolerant <br /><br />-sofia<br /><br />_<br /><br />I think the most intriguing part of this book was actually the art, not the poetry. But the drawings by themselves are just fine, and the poetry by itself is just okay, and together they're pretty mediocre. But still. It's food for thought, I guess. <br /><br />_<br /><br />you gave me<br />an apple<br />and i threw it<br />at your face<br /><br />- sofia<br /><br />_<br /><br />Overall, I thought this was a really gimmicky book of poems. It was just an "artistic way" of scribbling that I felt was contrived instead of beautiful. <br /><br />_<br /><br />i stayed at <br />a bed and breakfast<br />the room had no bed<br />but they still<br />brought me an egg<br /><br />- sofia</span>

<div id="review_2041575565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2041575565" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22104588-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498412758p2/22104588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041575565?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/22104588-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041575565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17435286498505872897"><b>This is total tumblr porn.</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23513349.Milk_and_Honey' title='Milk and Honey by Rupi Kaur' rel='nofollow noopener'>Milk and Honey</a> is pretty much a dream come true for emo fourteen-year-old girls who spend their spare time browsing deep, meaningful quotes written in pretty fonts like this one:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498595800i/23141914._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='430' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Also: I am going to argue that <b>this is not poetry.</b> Poetry is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7715.Robert_Frost' title='Robert Frost' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robert Frost</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe' title='Edgar Allan Poe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Edgar Allan Poe</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7440.Emily_Dickinson' title='Emily Dickinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Emily Dickinson</a>. I know poetry covers a wide range of styles, and I'm not saying <i>free verse</i> isn't poetry. I've read some excellent books by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins' title='Ellen Hopkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ellen Hopkins</a> written in free verse, expressing the lives</span>
  <span id="freeText17435286498505872897" style="display:none"><b>This is total tumblr porn.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23513349.Milk_and_Honey" title="Milk and Honey by Rupi Kaur" rel="nofollow noopener">Milk and Honey</a> is pretty much a dream come true for emo fourteen-year-old girls who spend their spare time browsing deep, meaningful quotes written in pretty fonts like this one:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498595800i/23141914._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="430" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also: I am going to argue that <b>this is not poetry.</b> Poetry is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7715.Robert_Frost" title="Robert Frost" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Frost</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">Edgar Allan Poe</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7440.Emily_Dickinson" title="Emily Dickinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily Dickinson</a>. I know poetry covers a wide range of styles, and I'm not saying <i>free verse</i> isn't poetry. I've read some excellent books by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins" title="Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Hopkins</a> written in free verse, expressing the lives of troubled teens better than most authors could. The writing in this book is barely even free verse. It's a collection of short sentences, words really, broken into segments.<br><br><b>i could write<br>a sentence<br>in small-caps<br>and keep hitting enter<br>so it looks cool<br>but that does not make it poetry</b><br><br>It really concerns me that this is a New York Times bestseller. Is this what people think of poetry nowadays? Granted, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23513349.Milk_and_Honey" title="Milk and Honey by Rupi Kaur" rel="nofollow noopener">Milk and Honey</a> did tackle a lot of tough subjects like abuse, heartbreak, and self-healing, but the poor quality of writing distracted from the message.<br><br>Some of the verses were outright laughable:<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>when i am sad<br>i don’t cry i pour<br>when i am happy<br>i don’t smile i glow<br>when i am angry<br>i don’t yell i burn</blockquote>
</i><br>And this one is just too good:<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>the goddess between your legs<br>makes mouths water</blockquote>
</i><br>Did you really just call women's reproductive organs a "goddess"? I'm still cracking up.<br><br>Also, why is this book so against women shaving? It acts like men hate hairy women but do you really think the average man sits around thinking, "I would totally date her, but she has leg hair." And don't feed me that "beauty standards are oppressing women" lie. No one is forcing women to go to the store, buy a razor, and shave. I shave because I like my legs to feel smooth. If you feel like your body hair empowers you, go you. If you feel like smooth skin empowers you, go you. I don't want to hear about it either way.<br><br>The truly sad thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23513349.Milk_and_Honey" title="Milk and Honey by Rupi Kaur" rel="nofollow noopener">Milk and Honey</a> is the author actually made some good points. Take this verse about women putting other women down:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>other women’s bodies<br>are not our battleground</i>
</blockquote><br>This is a serious issue that could have inspired a beautiful poem with a powerful message, but instead, the author wrote two lines that once again <b>made me feel like I was browsing a teen girl's tumblr page.</b> If you loved this book, cool beans. But I'd much rather read poetry where the writing doesn't retract from every point the author is trying to make.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17435286498505872897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1663188297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1663188297" />
    <a title="ellie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50105236-ellie"><img alt="ellie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523059874p2/50105236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1663188297?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ellie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ellie" href="/user/show/50105236-ellie">ellie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26877039-milk-and-honey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50105236-ellie?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50105236-ellie?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1663188297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16742030640886739071">To be simply put, this isn't a book meant to be loved or raved about. It is just meant to be read.<br/><br/>I feel as if the people giving it three stars or so went in expecting it to ravish them, thrill them but it was not meant for that. Why on earth would you seek something so much more from a book that was written so truthfully, with feelings so raw that the hurt and the bitterness and the sorrows behind the words will never dull? <br/><br/>This was her story. She isn't asking for you to judge if it's "exciting</span>
  <span id="freeText16742030640886739071" style="display:none">To be simply put, this isn't a book meant to be loved or raved about. It is just meant to be read.<br /><br />I feel as if the people giving it three stars or so went in expecting it to ravish them, thrill them but it was not meant for that. Why on earth would you seek something so much more from a book that was written so truthfully, with feelings so raw that the hurt and the bitterness and the sorrows behind the words will never dull? <br /><br />This was her story. She isn't asking for you to judge if it's "exciting" enough because it's not a fiction meant to be critiqued. Life isn't always "okay and then what?" Sometimes you can get stuck before you even try to move on.<br /><br /><i>if you were born with<br />the weakness to fall<br />you were born with<br />the strength to rise</i><br /><br />I am so moved by this. These were words she had woven out for herself and now we are allowed to read them and take them to our hearts, too.<br /><br /><i>you tell me to quiet down cause<br />my opinions make me less beautiful<br />but i was not made with a fire in my belly<br />so i could be put out<br />i was not made with a lightness on my tongue<br />so i could be easy to swallow<br />i was made heavy<br />half blade and half silk<br />difficult to forget and not easy<br />for the mind to follow</i><br /><br />Honestly, I am a young woman, a college student, surrounded by women who dumb themselves down and go out of their way to impress boys-because they think that'll give them happiness, in the end, and it may, but it will be what they think happiness is rather than what it actually is. But I've never felt more alive than when I was happy with myself, even if it was a small thing. And this poetry encourages self love beyond anything. It normalizes it. You can't get anywhere in life if you're holding yourself back. <br /><br />The doodles were so wonderful! Sincerely, they made me want to rip out the pages and put them up on my walls so I can look at them and remind myself of what is and what isn't and how I should grow, too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16742030640886739071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2260919231" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2260919231" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2260919231?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2260919231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16275929527739319724">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>Wow.<br/><br/>I really didn't know what to expect when I picked up Rupi Kaur's exquisite collection of poetry and prose. Poetry is often hit or miss with me—I totally appreciate it as an art form but sometimes I just don't get it. (I'm as creative as the next person, but sometimes my brain is tired and just wants to be told what something means rather than struggle to decode it. Sorry, I'm a Neanderthal.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Milk and Honey</i>
</b> is about happiness and despair, hurt and joy, love and sadness, and findi</span>
  <span id="freeText16275929527739319724" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />Wow.<br /><br />I really didn't know what to expect when I picked up Rupi Kaur's exquisite collection of poetry and prose. Poetry is often hit or miss with me—I totally appreciate it as an art form but sometimes I just don't get it. (I'm as creative as the next person, but sometimes my brain is tired and just wants to be told what something means rather than struggle to decode it. Sorry, I'm a Neanderthal.)<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Milk and Honey</i>
</b> is about happiness and despair, hurt and joy, love and sadness, and finding the strength to overcome your struggles. It is at times erotic, poignant, empowering, harrowing, and a celebration of all of the amazing qualities of women. Divided into four chapters—the hurting, the loving, the breaking, and the healing—each deals with a different step in relationships, both with someone else and with yourself.<br /><br /><i>most importantly love<br />like it's the only thing you know how<br />at the end of the day all this<br />means nothing<br />this page<br />where you're sitting<br />your degree<br />your job<br />the money<br />nothing even matters<br />except love and human connection<br />who you loved<br />and how deeply you loved them<br />how you touched the people around you<br />and how much you gave them</i><br /><br />Some of the poems are accompanied by small illustrations. I'd imagine that the print version of this book would make a beautiful gift for someone; I'm not sure if I missed out on something reading it on my Kindle, because I'm not 100 percent sure if each separate page is a separate poem or if the book is just laid out strangely. (I am also not quite sure if only some of the poems have titles or if each poem has its title at the end, meaning the stanzas between titled pages represent one poem.)<br /><br />Kaur is an absolutely dazzling writer. Her words evoke emotion, sexuality, femininity, anger, and hope. While perhaps some of this resonates more for women than for men, I still found this incredibly touching, incredibly moving, incredibly motivating, and at times simply breathtaking.<br /><br /><i>you might not have been my first love<br />but you were the love that made<br />all the other loves<br />irrelevant</i><br /><br />This collection won't be for everyone. You need to be willing to put aside conventional notions of punctuation, capitalization, and the way sentences are divided. But more than that, you need to be willing to be vulnerable, to listen to Kaur's messages, and feel the feelings she is trying to convey. If you can do that, you will be richly rewarded by the beauty of <b>
  <i>Milk and Honey</i>
</b>.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2017 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16275929527739319724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12761892069255610538" style="display:none">Sigh...   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2118876439?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Trevino" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Trevino" href="/user/show/52992135-james-trevino">James Trevino</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2118876439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13721093502189795506">Maybe I am not the most apt person to give an opinion on this, but I will throw in my 2 cents anyway.<br/><br/>First of all, I can't even remember the last time I read poetry. It is simply not that enjoyable to me. But I picked this up after seeing it on my Instagram feed a couple hundred times. I expected to be easily bored by it, but I read it in one sitting. Not that hard since the book is quite short and has lot of drawings, but still. I was surprised!<br/><br/>Milk and honey may be poetry (for the most part), </span>
  <span id="freeText13721093502189795506" style="display:none">Maybe I am not the most apt person to give an opinion on this, but I will throw in my 2 cents anyway.<br /><br />First of all, I can't even remember the last time I read poetry. It is simply not that enjoyable to me. But I picked this up after seeing it on my Instagram feed a couple hundred times. I expected to be easily bored by it, but I read it in one sitting. Not that hard since the book is quite short and has lot of drawings, but still. I was surprised!<br /><br />Milk and honey may be poetry (for the most part), but it tells a very cohesive story. A very powerful and moving story too. It is ultimately a book about hardships and empowerment and in my humble opinion, although obviously directed towards women, the message of self loving can apply to anyone, woman or man.<br /><br />The drawings were simple and gorgeous. Actually, the book felt a lot like going through a writer's Instagram feed if that makes any sense. <br /><br />All in all, a really nice read.<br />*<br />*<br />*<br />P.S.- On the funny side of things, this line ('the goddess between your legs makes mouths water') made me laugh so hard because it reminded me of Fifty Shades of Grey :))</span>

<div id="review_2118878051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2118878051" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Sagan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53505099-elizabeth-sagan"><img alt="Elizabeth Sagan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527068343p2/53505099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2118878051?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Sagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Sagan" href="/user/show/53505099-elizabeth-sagan">Elizabeth Sagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2118878051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17562422859256971849"><i> milk and honey </i> makes you grateful for your love of reading because it makes you understand how powerful words can be. It fills you with peace, acceptance and joy. You know that moment when you read something and you think „I needed years and a lot of pain to come to the same conclusion, if only I would have read this book earlier, it tells everything with such clarity”. I will recommend it to anyone who’s sad, depressed, down, heartbroken or lost. Basically the message is <i> accept your flaws, m</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17562422859256971849" style="display:none"><i> milk and honey </i> makes you grateful for your love of reading because it makes you understand how powerful words can be. It fills you with peace, acceptance and joy. You know that moment when you read something and you think „I needed years and a lot of pain to come to the same conclusion, if only I would have read this book earlier, it tells everything with such clarity”. I will recommend it to anyone who’s sad, depressed, down, heartbroken or lost. Basically the message is <i> accept your flaws, move on, life is flux, don’t let anyone make you feel unworthy. Be a shark. A nice, feminine, gentle shark. But a shark. </i><br />*<br /><i> You are every hope I’ve ever had in human form. </i><br />**<br /><i> Love knows life has been hard enough already </i><br />****<br /><i> You said, if it is meant to be, fate will bring us back together. [...] It’s us you fool. We’re the only ones that can bring us together.[...] Isn’t it such a tragic thing. When you can see it so clearly but the other person doesn’t. </i><br />*****<br /><i> Don’t mistake salt for sugar if he wants to be with you he will it’s that simple </i><br />******<br /><i> You’d rather have the darkest parts of him than have nothing </i><br />*******<br /><i> You whisper I love you What you mean is I don’t want you to leave </i><br />********<br /><i> Like I am supposed to be proud you picked me </i><br />*******<br /><i> But I swear you will get through the hurt will pass as it always does </i><br />******<br /><i> Nothing even matters except love and human connection </i><br />*****<br /><i> You have to stop searching for why at some point you have to leave it alone </i><br />****<br /><i> If you are not enough for yourself you will never be enough for someone else </i><br />***<br /><i> terrifies me most is how we foam at the mouth with envy when others succeed but sigh in relief when they are failing </i><br />**<br />I’ve heard THE PRINCESS SAVE HERSELF IN THIS ONE and FORTY RULES OF LOVE are similar to milk and honey.<br />*</span>
  <a data-text-id="17562422859256971849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1837777651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837777651" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1837777651?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1837777651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4675013819235681366"><blockquote>
  <i>love is not cruel <br/>we are cruel<br/>love is not a game<br/>we have made a game<br/>out of love</i>
</blockquote> <br/>I can't believe it took me so long to finally read this poetry collection, after shivering over so much of Rupi's online poetry snippets over the years, but here we are, and it was... captivating? Painful? Beautiful? Perfect?<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>what i miss most is how you loved me. but what i didn't know was how you loved me had so much to do with the person i was. it was a reflection of everything i gave to you.<br/><br/><b>how cruel i was to</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4675013819235681366" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>love is not cruel <br />we are cruel<br />love is not a game<br />we have made a game<br />out of love</i>
</blockquote> <br />I can't believe it took me so long to finally read this poetry collection, after shivering over so much of Rupi's online poetry snippets over the years, but here we are, and it was... captivating? Painful? Beautiful? Perfect?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>what i miss most is how you loved me. but what i didn't know was how you loved me had so much to do with the person i was. it was a reflection of everything i gave to you.<br /><br /><b>how cruel i was to myself. giving you credit for my warmth simply because you had felt it.</b></i>
</blockquote><br />I feel that this is a poetry collection that will be different things for different people, but for me, it was a love story written for those of us who have survived abusive relationships, who have moved on and learned to love ourselves despite the lies we were fed. If you've ever left a toxic relationship, friendship, situation, whatever - do you remember the first time you realized things weren't your fault? How it felt like the first breath of air after far too long underwater? <b>That's what this collection felt like for me.</b> It reminded me of how far I've come, and how strong I really am.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>the next time he<br />points out the<br />hair on your legs is<br />growing back remind<br />that boy your body<br />is not his home<br />he is a guest<br />warn him to<br />never outstep<br />his welcome<br />again</i>
</blockquote><br />Even better, this collection is so shamelessly, wholly feminist in nature and I cannot imagine <i>not</i> feeling empowered by the words Rupi writes. She is so proud of her womanhood and it's a contagious feeling.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>our backs<br />tell stories<br />no books have<br />the spine to<br />carry<br /><br />- women of color</i>
</blockquote><br />Finally, this poetry is an ode to people of color everywhere, and the ways their beauty, their experiences, and their livelihoods should not - and <b>
  <i>can not</i>
</b> - ever be taken away by prejudices of an ugly, bleak world.<br /><br /><b>Content warnings:</b> abuse, sexual assault, depression, loneliness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4675013819235681366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1756487203" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756487203" />
    <a title="Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23179211-riley"><img alt="Riley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601446413p2/23179211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756487203?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Riley" href="/user/show/23179211-riley">Riley</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=diverse-recs">diverse-recs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756487203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5078368626220488930">This was good, not great. Maybe I expected more because this has been recommended so much. <br/>It is split into 4 parts (the hurting, the loving, the breaking & the healing)<br/><i>The hurting</i> section was great. There was a lot about negative fatherly figures that was easy for me to relate to. I didn't really enjoy <i>the loving</i> section. I don't get much out of poems about falling in love so this part was just meh. <i>The breaking</i> was underwhelming. A lot of repeating the same basic thought "you don't need a man"</span>
  <span id="freeText5078368626220488930" style="display:none">This was good, not great. Maybe I expected more because this has been recommended so much. <br />It is split into 4 parts (the hurting, the loving, the breaking &amp; the healing)<br /><i>The hurting</i> section was great. There was a lot about negative fatherly figures that was easy for me to relate to. I didn't really enjoy <i>the loving</i> section. I don't get much out of poems about falling in love so this part was just meh. <i>The breaking</i> was underwhelming. A lot of repeating the same basic thought "you don't need a man" <br />I think I get it. <br />The last section again was underwhelming. I just wasn't overly impressed by any of the poems. Even the ones I saved were just okay and would not have made an impression on me had they been in a poetry book that I love. <br />It's a quick read but I think this collection is better for beginners to poetry who are looking for something more straightforward and easy to understand.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5078368626220488930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6p/kT3XZ74tA3Onmp5LgN+sNyopZiZhd32Uq4epCT7vDzrDakZDefs5LIc+Oi4g7OZe6cYsNdseeSMOFX2VI6Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PZ8S2A64NfYn4ZCooc/FgagEg0hUE2IqSN0pxNVnBHkUzkZN6vEEA6l2WIGI1q2Nep7zs4aXjLAJ8MCgYEADKw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16327532975636426201">Rupi Kaur is a writer and artist based in Toronto, Canada. With a focus in poetry, she released her first book of prose and poems in November 2014. Throughout her poetry, photography, illustrations, and creative direction she engages with themes of femininity, love, loss, trauma, and healing. When she is not writing or creating art, she is travelling internationally to perform her spoken word poet</span>
  <span id="freeText16327532975636426201" style="display:none">Rupi Kaur is a writer and artist based in Toronto, Canada. With a focus in poetry, she released her first book of prose and poems in November 2014. Throughout her poetry, photography, illustrations, and creative direction she engages with themes of femininity, love, loss, trauma, and healing. When she is not writing or creating art, she is travelling internationally to perform her spoken word poetry, as well as hosting writing workshops. You can find more of her work at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.rupikaur.com">www.rupikaur.com</a> </span>
